syntax for GitHub Actions","intro":"\u003cp\u003eA workflow is a configurable automated process made up of one or more jobs. You must create a YAML file to define your workflow configuration.\u003c/p\u003e","effectiveDate":"","renderedPage":"\u003ch2 id=\"about-yaml-syntax-for-workflows\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#about-yaml-syntax-for-workflows\"\u003eAbout YAML syntax for workflows\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWorkflow files use YAML syntax, and must have either a \u003ccode\u003e.yml\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003e.yaml\u003c/code\u003e file extension. If you're new to YAML and want to learn more, see \u003ca href=\"https://learnxinyminutes.com/docs/yaml/\"\u003eLearn YAML in Y minutes\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou must store workflow files in the \u003ccode\u003e.github/workflows\u003c/code\u003e directory of your repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"name\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#name\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ename\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe name of the workflow. GitHub displays the names of your workflows under your repository's \"Actions\" tab. If you omit \u003ccode\u003ename\u003c/code\u003e, GitHub displays the workflow file path relative to the root of the repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"run-name\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#run-name\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003erun-name\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe name for workflow runs generated from the workflow. GitHub displays the workflow run name in the list of workflow runs on your repository's \"Actions\" tab. If \u003ccode\u003erun-name\u003c/code\u003e is omitted or is only whitespace, then the run name is set to event-specific information for the workflow run. For example, for a workflow triggered by a \u003ccode\u003epush\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e event, it is set as the commit message or the title of the pull request.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis value can include expressions and can reference the \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#github-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003egithub\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#inputs-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003einputs\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e contexts.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-of-run-name\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-of-run-name\"\u003eExample of \u003ccode\u003erun-name\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003erun-name:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eDeploy\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eto\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003einputs.deploy\_target\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eby\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e@${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.actor\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"on\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#on\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eon\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo automatically trigger a workflow, use \u003ccode\u003eon\u003c/code\u003e to define which events can cause the workflow to run. For a list of available events, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/events-that-trigger-workflows\"\u003eEvents that trigger workflows\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can define single or multiple events that can trigger a workflow, or set a time schedule. You can also restrict the execution of a workflow to only occur for specific files, tags, or branch changes. These options are described in the following sections.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"using-a-single-event\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#using-a-single-event\"\u003eUsing a single event\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, a workflow with the following \u003ccode\u003eon\u003c/code\u003e value will run when a push is made to any branch in the workflow's repository:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003epush\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"using-multiple-events\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#using-multiple-events\"\u003eUsing multiple events\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can specify a single event or multiple events. For example, a workflow with the following \u003ccode\u003eon\u003c/code\u003e value will run when a push is made to any branch in the repository or when someone forks the repository:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003epush\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003efork\u003c/span\u003e]\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you specify multiple events, only one of those events needs to occur to trigger your workflow. If multiple triggering events for your workflow occur at the same time, multiple workflow runs will be triggered.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"using-activity-types\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#using-activity-types\"\u003eUsing activity types\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSome events have activity types that give you more control over when your workflow should run. Use \u003ccode\u003eon.\u0026#x3C;event\_name\u003e.types\u003c/code\u003e to define the type of event activity that will trigger a workflow run.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the \u003ccode\u003eissue\_comment\u003c/code\u003e event has the \u003ccode\u003ecreated\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eedited\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003edeleted\u003c/code\u003e activity types. If your workflow triggers on the \u003ccode\u003elabel\u003c/code\u003e event, it will run whenever a label is created, edited, or deleted. If you specify the \u003ccode\u003ecreated\u003c/code\u003e activity type for the \u003ccode\u003elabel\u003c/code\u003e event, your workflow will run when a label is created but not when a label is edited or deleted.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003elabel:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003etypes:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ecreated\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you specify multiple activity types, only one of those event activity types needs to occur to trigger your workflow. If multiple triggering event activity types for your workflow occur at the same time, multiple workflow runs will be triggered. For example, the following workflow triggers when an issue is opened or labeled. If an issue with two labels is opened, three workflow runs will start: one for the issue opened event and two for the two issue labeled events.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eissues:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003etypes:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eopened\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003elabeled\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor more information about each event and their activity types, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/events-that-trigger-workflows\"\u003eEvents that trigger workflows\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"using-filters\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#using-filters\"\u003eUsing filters\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSome events have filters that give you more control over when your workflow should run.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the \u003ccode\u003epush\u003c/code\u003e event has a \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e filter that causes your workflow to run only when a push to a branch that matches the \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e filter occurs, instead of when any push occurs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'releases/\*\*'\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"using-activity-types-and-filters-with-multiple-events\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#using-activity-types-and-filters-with-multiple-events\"\u003eUsing activity types and filters with multiple events\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you specify activity types or filters for an event and your workflow triggers on multiple events, you must configure each event separately. You must append a colon (\u003ccode\u003e:\u003c/code\u003e) to all events, including events without configuration.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, a workflow with the following \u003ccode\u003eon\u003c/code\u003e value will run when:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA label is created\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA push is made to the \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e branch in the repository\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA push is made to a GitHub Pages-enabled branch\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003elabel:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003etypes:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ecreated\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epage\_build:\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"onevent\_nametypes\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#onevent\_nametypes\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eon.\u0026#x3C;event\_name\u003e.types\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003eon.\u0026#x3C;event\_name\u003e.types\u003c/code\u003e to define the type of activity that will trigger a workflow run. Most GitHub events are triggered by more than one type of activity. For example, the \u003ccode\u003elabel\u003c/code\u003e is triggered when a label is \u003ccode\u003ecreated\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eedited\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003edeleted\u003c/code\u003e. The \u003ccode\u003etypes\u003c/code\u003e keyword enables you to narrow down activity that causes the workflow to run. When only one activity type triggers a webhook event, the \u003ccode\u003etypes\u003c/code\u003e keyword is unnecessary.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use an array of event \u003ccode\u003etypes\u003c/code\u003e. For more information about each event and their activity types, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/events-that-trigger-workflows#available-events\"\u003eEvents that trigger workflows\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003elabel:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003etypes:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ecreated\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eedited\u003c/span\u003e]\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"onpull\_requestpull\_request\_targetbranchesbranches-ignore\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#onpull\_requestpull\_request\_targetbranchesbranches-ignore\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eon.\u0026#x3C;pull\_request|pull\_request\_target\u003e.\u0026#x3C;branches|branches-ignore\u003e\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen using the \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\_target\u003c/code\u003e events, you can configure a workflow to run only for pull requests that target specific branches.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse the \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e filter when you want to include branch name patterns or when you want to both include and exclude branch names patterns. Use the \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e filter when you only want to exclude branch name patterns. You cannot use both the \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e filters for the same event in a workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you define both \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#onpushpull\_requestpull\_request\_targetpathspaths-ignore\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, the workflow will only run when both filters are satisfied.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e keywords accept glob patterns that use characters like \u003ccode\u003e\*\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e\*\*\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e+\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e?\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e and others to match more than one branch name. If a name contains any of these characters and you want a literal match, you need to escape each of these special characters with \u003ccode\u003e\\\u003c/code\u003e. For more information about glob patterns, see the \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#filter-pattern-cheat-sheet\"\u003eWorkflow syntax for GitHub Actions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-including-branches\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-including-branches\"\u003eExample: Including branches\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe patterns defined in \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e are evaluated against the Git ref's name. For example, the following workflow would run whenever there is a \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e event for a pull request targeting:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA branch named \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e (\u003ccode\u003erefs/heads/main\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA branch named \u003ccode\u003emona/octocat\u003c/code\u003e (\u003ccode\u003erefs/heads/mona/octocat\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA branch whose name starts with \u003ccode\u003ereleases/\u003c/code\u003e, like \u003ccode\u003ereleases/10\u003c/code\u003e (\u003ccode\u003erefs/heads/releases/10\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epull\_request:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003e# Sequence of patterns matched against refs/heads\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'mona/octocat'\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'releases/\*\*'\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf a workflow is skipped due to branch filtering, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#onpushpull\_requestpull\_request\_targetpathspaths-ignore\"\u003epath filtering\u003c/a\u003e, or a \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/managing-workflow-runs/skipping-workflow-runs\"\u003ecommit message\u003c/a\u003e, then checks associated with that workflow will remain in a \"Pending\" state. A pull request that requires those checks to be successful will be blocked from merging.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-excluding-branches\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-excluding-branches\"\u003eExample: Excluding branches\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen a pattern matches the \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e pattern, the workflow will not run. The patterns defined in \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e are evaluated against the Git ref's name. For example, the following workflow would run whenever there is a \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e event unless the pull request is targeting:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA branch named \u003ccode\u003emona/octocat\u003c/code\u003e (\u003ccode\u003erefs/heads/mona/octocat\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA branch whose name matches \u003ccode\u003ereleases/\*\*-alpha\u003c/code\u003e, like \u003ccode\u003ereleases/beta/3-alpha\u003c/code\u003e (\u003ccode\u003erefs/heads/releases/beta/3-alpha\u003c/code\u003e) \u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epull\_request:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003e# Sequence of patterns matched against refs/heads\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches-ignore:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'mona/octocat'\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'releases/\*\*-alpha'\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-including-and-excluding-branches\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-including-and-excluding-branches\"\u003eExample: Including and excluding branches\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou cannot use \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e to filter the same event in a single workflow. If you want to both include and exclude branch patterns for a single event, use the \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e filter along with the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character to indicate which branches should be excluded.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you define a branch with the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character, you must also define at least one branch without the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character. If you only want to exclude branches, use \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e instead.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe order that you define patterns matters.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA matching negative pattern (prefixed with \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e) after a positive match will exclude the Git ref.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA matching positive pattern after a negative match will include the Git ref again.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe following workflow will run on \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e events for pull requests that target \u003ccode\u003ereleases/10\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003ereleases/beta/mona\u003c/code\u003e, but not for pull requests that target \u003ccode\u003ereleases/10-alpha\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003ereleases/beta/3-alpha\u003c/code\u003e because the negative pattern \u003ccode\u003e!releases/\*\*-alpha\u003c/code\u003e follows the positive pattern. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epull\_request:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'releases/\*\*'\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'!releases/\*\*-alpha'\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"onpushbranchestagsbranches-ignoretags-ignore\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#onpushbranchestagsbranches-ignoretags-ignore\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eon.push.\u0026#x3C;branches|tags|branches-ignore|tags-ignore\u003e\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen using the \u003ccode\u003epush\u003c/code\u003e event, you can configure a workflow to run on specific branches or tags.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse the \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e filter when you want to include branch name patterns or when you want to both include and exclude branch names patterns. Use the \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e filter when you only want to exclude branch name patterns. You cannot use both the \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e filters for the same event in a workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse the \u003ccode\u003etags\u003c/code\u003e filter when you want to include tag name patterns or when you want to both include and exclude tag names patterns. Use the \u003ccode\u003etags-ignore\u003c/code\u003e filter when you only want to exclude tag name patterns. You cannot use both the \u003ccode\u003etags\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003etags-ignore\u003c/code\u003e filters for the same event in a workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you define only \u003ccode\u003etags\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003etags-ignore\u003c/code\u003e or only \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e, the workflow won't run for events affecting the undefined Git ref. If you define neither \u003ccode\u003etags\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003etags-ignore\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e, the workflow will run for events affecting either branches or tags. If you define both \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#onpushpull\_requestpull\_request\_targetpathspaths-ignore\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, the workflow will only run when both filters are satisfied.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003etags\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003etags-ignore\u003c/code\u003e keywords accept glob patterns that use characters like \u003ccode\u003e\*\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e\*\*\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e+\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e?\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e and others to match more than one branch or tag name. If a name contains any of these characters and you want a literal match, you need to \u003cem\u003eescape\u003c/em\u003e each of these special characters with \u003ccode\u003e\\\u003c/code\u003e. For more information about glob patterns, see the \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#filter-pattern-cheat-sheet\"\u003eWorkflow syntax for GitHub Actions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-including-branches-and-tags\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-including-branches-and-tags\"\u003eExample: Including branches and tags\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe patterns defined in \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003etags\u003c/code\u003e are evaluated against the Git ref's name. For example, the following workflow would run whenever there is a \u003ccode\u003epush\u003c/code\u003e event to:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA branch named (\u003ccode\u003erefs/tags/v1.9.1\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan to:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA branch named \u003ccode\u003emona/octocat\u003c/code\u003e (\u003ccode\u003erefs/heads/mona/octocat\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA (\u003ccode\u003erefs/tags/v1.9\u003c/code\u003e)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan \u003cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003e# Sequence of patterns matched against refs/tags\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003etags-ignore:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ev2\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ev1.\*\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-including-and-excluding-branches-and-tags\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-including-and-excluding-branches-and-tags\"\u003eExample: Including and excluding branches and tags\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can't use \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e to filter the same event in a single workflow. Similarly, you can't use \u003ccode\u003etags\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003etags-ignore\u003c/code\u003e to filter the same event in a single workflow. If you want to both include and exclude branch or tag patterns for a single event, use the \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003etags\u003c/code\u003e filter along with the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character to indicate which branches or tags should be excluded.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you define a branch with the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character, you must also define at least one branch without the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character. If you only want to exclude branches, use \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e instead. Similarly, if you define a tag with the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character, you must also define at least one tag without the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character. If you only want to exclude tags, use \u003ccode\u003etags-ignore\u003c/code\u003e instead.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe order that you define patterns matters.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA matching negative pattern (prefixed with \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e) after a positive match will exclude the Git ref.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA matching positive pattern after a negative match will include the Git ref again.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe following workflow will run on pushes to \u003ccode\u003ereleases/10\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003ereleases/beta/mona\u003c/code\u003e, but not on \u003ccode\u003ereleases/10-alpha\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003ereleases/beta/3-alpha\u003c/code\u003e because the negative pattern \u003ccode\u003e!releases/\*\*-alpha\u003c/code\u003e follows the positive pattern. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'releases/\*\*'\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'!releases/\*\*-alpha'\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"onpushpull\_requestpull\_request\_targetpathspaths-ignore\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#onpushpull\_requestpull\_request\_targetpathspaths-ignore\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eon.\u0026#x3C;push|pull\_request|pull\_request\_target\u003e.\u0026#x3C;paths|paths-ignore\u003e\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen using the \u003ccode\u003epush\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e events, you can configure a workflow to run based on what file paths are changed. Path filters are not evaluated for pushes of tags.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse the \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e filter when you want to include file path patterns or when you want to both include and exclude file path patterns. Use the \u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e filter when you only want to exclude file path patterns. You cannot use both the \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e filters for the same event in a workflow. If you want to both include and exclude path patterns for a single event, use the \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e filter prefixed with the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character to indicate which paths should be excluded.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nThe order that you define \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e patterns matters:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA matching negative pattern (prefixed with \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e) after a positive match will exclude the path.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA matching positive pattern after a negative match will include the path again.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you define both \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e, the workflow will only run when both filters are satisfied.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e keywords accept glob patterns that use the \u003ccode\u003e\*\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e\*\*\u003c/code\u003e wildcard characters to match more than one path name. For more information, see the \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#filter-pattern-cheat-sheet\"\u003eWorkflow syntax for GitHub Actions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-including-paths\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-including-paths\"\u003eExample: Including paths\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf at least one path matches a pattern in the \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e filter, the workflow runs. For example, the following workflow would run anytime you push a JavaScript file (\u003ccode\u003e.js\u003c/code\u003e).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epaths:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'\*\*.js'\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf a workflow is skipped due to path filtering, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#onpull\_requestpull\_request\_targetbranchesbranches-ignore\"\u003ebranch filtering\u003c/a\u003e, or a \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/managing-workflow-runs/skipping-workflow-runs\"\u003ecommit message\u003c/a\u003e, then checks associated with that workflow will remain in a \"Pending\" state. A pull request that requires those checks to be successful will be blocked from merging.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-excluding-paths\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-excluding-paths\"\u003eExample: Excluding paths\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen all the path names match patterns in \u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e, the workflow will not run. If any path names do not match patterns in \u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e, even if some path names match the patterns, the workflow will run.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA workflow with the following path filter will only run on \u003ccode\u003epush\u003c/code\u003e events that include at least one file outside the \u003ccode\u003edocs\u003c/code\u003e directory at the root of the repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epaths-ignore:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'docs/\*\*'\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-including-and-excluding-paths\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-including-and-excluding-paths\"\u003eExample: Including and excluding paths\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou cannot use \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e to filter the same event in a single workflow. If you want to both include and exclude path patterns for a single event, use the \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e filter prefixed with the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character to indicate which paths should be excluded.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you define a path with the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character, you must also define at least one path without the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character. If you only want to exclude paths, use \u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e instead.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe order that you define \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e patterns matters:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA matching negative pattern (prefixed with \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e) after a positive match will exclude the path.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA matching positive pattern after a negative match will include the path again.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis example runs anytime the \u003ccode\u003epush\u003c/code\u003e event includes a file in the \u003ccode\u003esub-project\u003c/code\u003e directory or its subdirectories, unless the file is in the \u003ccode\u003esub-project/docs\u003c/code\u003e directory. For example, a push that changed \u003ccode\u003esub-project/index.js\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003esub-project/src/index.js\u003c/code\u003e will trigger a workflow run, but a push changing only \u003ccode\u003esub-project/docs/readme.md\u003c/code\u003e will not.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epaths:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'sub-project/\*\*'\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'!sub-project/docs/\*\*'\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"git-diff-comparisons\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#git-diff-comparisons\"\u003eGit diff comparisons\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nIf you push more than 1,000 commits, or if GitHub does not generate the diff due to a timeout, the workflow will always run.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe filter determines if a workflow should run by evaluating the changed files and running them against the \u003ccode\u003epaths-ignore\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003epaths\u003c/code\u003e list. If there are no files changed, the workflow will not run.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eGitHub generates the list of changed files using two-dot diffs for pushes and three-dot diffs for pull requests:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePull requests:\u003c/strong\u003e Three-dot diffs are a comparison between the most recent version of the topic branch and the commit where the topic branch was last synced with the base branch.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePushes to existing branches:\u003c/strong\u003e A two-dot diff compares the head and base SHAs directly with each other.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003ePushes to new branches:\u003c/strong\u003e A two-dot diff against the parent of the ancestor of the deepest commit pushed.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nDiffs are limited to 300 files. If there are files changed that aren't matched in the first 300 files returned by the filter, the workflow will not run. You may need to create more specific filters so that the workflow will run automatically.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/pull-requests/collaborating-with-pull-requests/proposing-changes-to-your-work-with-pull-requests/about-comparing-branches-in-pull-requests\"\u003eAbout comparing branches in pull requests\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"onschedule\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#onschedule\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eon.schedule\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use \u003ccode\u003eon.schedule\u003c/code\u003e to define a time schedule for your workflows.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ca href=\"https://pubs.opengroup.org/onlinepubs/9699919799/utilities/crontab.html#tag\_20\_25\_07\"\u003ePOSIX cron syntax\u003c/a\u003e to schedule workflows to run at specific times. By default, scheduled workflows run in UTC. You can optionally specify a timezone using an \u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List\_of\_tz\_database\_time\_zones\"\u003eIANA timezone string\u003c/a\u003e for timezone-aware scheduling. Scheduled workflows run on the latest commit on the default branch. The shortest interval you can run scheduled workflows is once every 5 minutes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nFor schedules that set \u003ccode\u003etimezone\u003c/code\u003e to a time zone that observes daylight saving time (DST), during DST spring-forward transitions, scheduled workflows in skipped hours advance to the next valid time. For example, a 2:30 AM schedule advances to 3:00 AM.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eCron syntax has five fields separated by a space, and each field represents a unit of time.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-text\"\u003e┌───────────── minute (0 - 59)\n│ ┌───────────── hour (0 - 23)\n│ │ ┌───────────── day of the month (1 - 31)\n│ │ │ ┌───────────── month (1 - 12 or JAN-DEC)\n│ │ │ │ ┌───────────── day of the week (0 - 6 or SUN-SAT)\n│ │ │ │ │\n\* \* \* \* \*\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use these operators in any of the five fields:\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\u003ctable aria-labelledby=\"onschedule\"\u003e\u003cthead\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eOperator\u003c/th\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eDescription\u003c/th\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eExample\u003c/th\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003c/thead\u003e\u003ctbody\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\*\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eAny value\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e15 \* \* \* \*\u003c/code\u003e runs at every minute 15 of every hour of every day.\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e,\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eValue list separator\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e2,10 4,5 \* \* \*\u003c/code\u003e runs at minute 2 and 10 of the 4th and 5th hour of every day.\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e-\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eRange of values\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e30 4-6 \* \* \*\u003c/code\u003e runs at minute 30 of the 4th, 5th, and 6th hour.\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e/\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eStep values\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e20/15 \* \* \* \*\u003c/code\u003e runs every 15 minutes starting from minute 20 through 59 (minutes 20, 35, and 50).\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003c/tbody\u003e\u003c/table\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis example triggers the workflow to run at 5:30 AM in the America/New\_York timezone every Monday through Friday:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eschedule:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecron:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'30 5 \* \* 1-5'\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003etimezone:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"America/New\_York\"\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA single workflow can be triggered by multiple \u003ccode\u003eschedule\u003c/code\u003e events. Access the \u003ccode\u003eschedule\u003c/code\u003e event that triggered the workflow through the \u003ccode\u003egithub.event.schedule\u003c/code\u003e context. This example triggers the workflow to run at 5:30 UTC every Monday-Thursday, and 17:30 UTC on Tuesdays and Thursdays, but skips the \u003ccode\u003eNot on Monday or Wednesday\u003c/code\u003e step on Monday and Wednesday.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eschedule:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecron:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'30 5 \* \* 1,3'\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecron:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen using the \u003ccode\u003eworkflow\_run\u003c/code\u003e event, you can specify what branches the triggering workflow must run on in order to trigger your workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e filters accept glob patterns that use characters like \u003ccode\u003e\*\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e\*\*\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e+\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e?\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e and others to match more than one branch name. If a name contains any of these characters and you want a literal match, you need to \u003cem\u003eescape\u003c/em\u003e each of these special characters with \u003ccode\u003e\\\u003c/code\u003e. For more information about glob patterns, see the \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#filter-pattern-cheat-sheet\"\u003eWorkflow syntax for GitHub Actions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, a workflow with the following trigger will only run when the workflow named \u003ccode\u003eBuild\u003c/code\u003e runs on a branch class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'releases/\*\*'\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA workflow with the following trigger will only run when the workflow named \u003ccode\u003eBuild\u003c/code\u003e runs on a branch that is not named \u003ccode\u003ecanary\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eworkflow\_run:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eworkflows:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"Build\"\u003c/span\u003e]\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003etypes:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003erequested\u003c/span\u003e]\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches-ignore:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"canary\"\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou cannot use both the \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ebranches-ignore\u003c/code\u003e filters for the same event in a workflow. If you want to both include and exclude branch patterns for a single event, use the \u003ccode\u003ebranches\u003c/code\u003e filter along with the \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e character to indicate which branches should be excluded.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe order that you define patterns matters.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA matching negative pattern (prefixed with \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e) after a positive match will exclude the branch.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA matching positive pattern after a negative match will include the branch again.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, a workflow with the following trigger will run when the workflow named \u003ccode\u003eBuild\u003c/code\u003e runs on a branch that is named \u003ccode\u003ereleases/10\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003ereleases/beta/mona\u003c/code\u003e but will not \u003ccode\u003ereleases/10-alpha\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003ereleases/beta/3-alpha\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen using the \u003ccode\u003eworkflow\_dispatch\u003c/code\u003e event, you can optionally specify inputs that are passed to the workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis trigger only receives events when the workflow file is on the default branch.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"onworkflow\_dispatchinputs\" For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#inputs-context\"\u003eContexts\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe workflow will also receive the inputs in the \u003ccode\u003egithub.event.inputs\u003c/code\u003e context. The information in the \u003ccode\u003einputs\u003c/code\u003e context and \u003ccode\u003egithub.event.inputs\u003c/code\u003e context is identical except that the \u003ccode\u003einputs\u003c/code\u003e context preserves Boolean values as Booleans instead of converting them to strings. The \u003ccode\u003echoice\u003c/code\u003e type resolves to a string and is a single selectable option.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe maximum number of top-level properties for aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA boolean specifying whether the input must be supplied.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"onworkflow\_dispatchinputsinput\_idtype\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#onworkflow\_dispatchinputsinput\_idtype\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eon.workflow\_dispatch.inputs.\u0026#x3C;input\_id\u003e.type\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe value of this parameter is a string specifying the data type of the input. This must be one of: \u003ccode\u003eboolean\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003echoice\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003enumber\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eenvironment\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003estring\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"permissions\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#permissions\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epermissions\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use \u003ccode\u003epermissions\u003c/code\u003e to modify the default permissions granted to the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e, adding or removing access as required, so that you only allow the minimum required access. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/security-guides/automatic-token-authentication#modifying-the-permissions-for-the-github\_token\"\u003eUse GITHUB\_TOKEN for authentication in workflows\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use \u003ccode\u003epermissions\u003c/code\u003e either as a top-level key, to apply to all jobs in the workflow, or within specific jobs. When you add the \u003ccode\u003epermissions\u003c/code\u003e key within a specific job, all actions and run commands within that job that use the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e gain the access rights you specify. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#jobsjob\_idpermissions\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.permissions\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOwners of an organization can restrict write access for the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e at the repository level. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/organizations/managing-organization-settings/disabling-or-limiting-github-actions-for-your-organization#setting-the-permissions-of-the-github\_token-for-your-organization\"\u003eDisabling or limiting GitHub Actions for your organization\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen a workflow is triggered by the \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/events-that-trigger-workflows#pull\_request\_target\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epull\_request\_target\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e event, the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e is granted read/write repository permission, even when it is triggered from a public fork. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/events-that-trigger-workflows#pull\_request\_target\"\u003eEvents that trigger workflows\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor each of the available permissions, shown in the table below, you can assign one of the access levels: \u003ccode\u003eread\u003c/code\u003e (if applicable), \u003ccode\u003ewrite\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003enone\u003c/code\u003e. \u003ccode\u003ewrite\u003c/code\u003e includes \u003ccode\u003eread\u003c/code\u003e. If you specify the access for any of these permissions, all of those that are not specified are set to \u003ccode\u003enone\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAvailable permissions and details of what each allows an action to do:\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\u003ctable aria-labelledby=\"permissions\"\u003e\u003cthead\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003ePermission\u003c/th\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eAllows an action using \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e to\u003c/th\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003c/thead\u003e\u003ctbody\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003eactions\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eWork with GitHub Actions. For example, \u003ccode\u003eactions: write\u003c/code\u003e permits an action to cancel a workflow run. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/security-guides/using-artifact-attestations-to-establish-provenance-for-builds\"\u003eUsing artifact attestations to establish provenance for builds\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003echecks\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eWork with check runs and check suites. For example, \u003ccode\u003echecks: write\u003c/code\u003e permits an action to create a check run. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/overview/permissions-required-for-github-apps?apiVersion=2022-11-28#repository-permissions-for-checks\"\u003ePermissions required for GitHub Apps\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003econtents\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eWork with the contents of the repository. For example, \u003ccode\u003econtents: read\u003c/code\u003e permits an action to list the commits, and \u003ccode\u003econtents: write\u003c/code\u003e allows the action to create a release. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/overview/permissions-required-for-github-apps?apiVersion=2022-11-28#repository-permissions-for-contents\"\u003ePermissions required for GitHub Apps\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003edeployments\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eWork with deployments. For example, \u003ccode\u003ediscussions: write\u003c/code\u003e permits an action to close or delete a discussion. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/graphql/guides/using-the-graphql-api-for-discussions\"\u003eUsing the GraphQL API for Discussions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003eid-token\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eFetch an OpenID Connect (OIDC) token. This requires \u003ccode\u003eid-token: write\u003c/code\u003e. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/deployment/security-hardening-your-deployments/about-security-hardening-with-openid-connect#updating-your-actions-for-oidc\"\u003eOpenID Connect\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003eissues\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eWork with issues. For example, \u003ccode\u003eissues: write\u003c/code\u003e permits an action to add a comment to an issue. aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use the \u003ccode\u003epermissions\u003c/code\u003e key to add and remove read permissions for forked repositories, but typically you can't grant write access. The exception to this behavior is where an admin user has selected the \u003cstrong\u003eSend write tokens to workflows from pull requests\u003c/strong\u003e option in the GitHub Actions settings. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/repositories/managing-your-repositorys-settings-and-features/enabling-features-for-your-repository/managing-github-actions-settings-for-a-repository#enabling-workflows-for-private-repository-forks\"\u003eManaging GitHub Actions settings for a repository\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"how-permissions-are-calculated-for-a-workflow-job\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#how-permissions-are-calculated-for-a-workflow-job\"\u003eHow permissions are calculated for a workflow job\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe permissions for the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e are initially set to the default setting for the enterprise, organization, or repository. If the default is set to the restricted permissions at any of these levels then this will apply to the relevant repositories. For example, if you choose the restricted default at the organization level then all repositories in that organization will use the restricted permissions as the default. The permissions are then adjusted based on any configuration within the workflow file, first at the workflow level and then at the job level. Finally, if the workflow was triggered by a pull request event other than \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\_target\u003c/code\u003e from a forked repository, and the \u003cstrong\u003eSend write tokens to workflows from pull requests\u003c/strong\u003e setting is not selected, the permissions are adjusted to change any write permissions to read only.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"setting-the-github\_token-permissions-for-all-jobs-in-a-workflow\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#setting-the-github\_token-permissions-for-all-jobs-in-a-workflow\"\u003eSetting the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e permissions for all jobs in a workflow\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can specify \u003ccode\u003epermissions\u003c/code\u003e at the top level of a workflow, so that the setting applies to all jobs in the workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"example-setting-the-github\_token-permissions-for-an-entire-workflow\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-setting-the-github\_token-permissions-for-an-entire-workflow\"\u003eExample: Setting the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e permissions for an entire workflow\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis example shows permissions being set for the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e that will apply to all jobs in the workflow. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#jobsjob\_idenv\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.env\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#jobsjob\_idstepsenv\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.steps[\*].env\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eVariables in the \u003ccode\u003eenv\u003c/code\u003e map cannot be defined in terms of other variables in the map.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen more than one environment variable is defined with the same name, GitHub uses the most specific variable. For example, a default setting defined in a job will override a default setting that has the same name defined in a workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-set-the-default-shell-and-working-directory\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-set-the-default-shell-and-working-directory\"\u003eExample: Set the default shell and working directory\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003edefaults:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003erun:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eshell:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ebash\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eworking-directory:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e./scripts\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"defaultsrunshell\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#defaultsrunshell\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003edefaults.run.shell\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003eshell\u003c/code\u003e to define the \u003ccode\u003eshell\u003c/code\u003e for a step. This keyword can reference several contexts. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#context-availability\"\u003eContexts\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\u003ctable aria-labelledby=\"defaultsrunshell\"\u003e\u003cthead\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eSupported platform\u003c/th\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eshell\u003c/code\u003e parameter\u003c/th\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eDescription\u003c/th\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eCommand run internally\u003c/th\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003c/thead\u003e\u003ctbody\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003eLinux / macOS\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eunspecified\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eThe default shell on non-Windows platforms. When specifying a bash shell on Windows, the bash shell included with Git for Windows is used.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003ebash --noprofile --norc -eo pipefail {0}\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003eAll\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003epwsh\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eThe PowerShell Core.
