For example, a default setting defined in a job will override a default setting that has the same name defined in a workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"defaultsrunworking-directory\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#defaultsrunworking-directory\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003edefaults.run.working-directory\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003eworking-directory\u003c/code\u003e to define the working directory for the \u003ccode\u003eshell\u003c/code\u003e for a step. This keyword can reference several contexts. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#context-availability\"\u003eContexts\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-success\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M8 1.5c-2.363 0-4 1.69-4 3.75 0 .984.424 1.625.984 2.304l.214.253c.223.264.47.556.673.848.284.411.537.896.621 1.49a.75.75 0 0 1-1.484.211c-.04-.282-.163-.547-.37-.847a8.456 8.456 0 0 0-.542-.68c-.084-.1-.173-.205-.268-.32C3.201 7.75 2.5 6.766 2.5 5.25 2.5 2.31 4.863 0 8 0s5.5 2.31 5.5 5.25c0 1.516-.701 2.5-1.328 3.259-.095.115-.184.22-.268.319-.207.245-.383.453-.541.681-.208.3-.33.565-.37.847a.751.751 0 0 1-1.485-.212c.084-.593.337-1.078.621-1.489.203-.292.45-.584.673-.848.075-.088.147-.173.213-.253.561-.679.985-1.32.985-2.304 0-2.06-1.637-3.75-4-3.75ZM5.75 12h4.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-4.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5ZM6 15.25a.75.75 0 0 1 .75-.75h2.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2.5a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eTip\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nEnsure the \u003ccode\u003eworking-directory\u003c/code\u003e you assign exists on the runner before you run your shell in it.\nWhen more than one default setting is defined with the same name, GitHub uses the most specific default setting. For example, a default setting defined in a job will override a default setting that has the same name defined in a workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"concurrency\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#concurrency\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e to ensure that only a single job or workflow using the same concurrency group will run at a time. A concurrency group can be any string or expression. The expression can only use \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#github-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003egithub\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#inputs-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003einputs\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#vars-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003evars\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e contexts. For more information about expressions, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/expressions\"\u003eEvaluate expressions in workflows and actions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can also specify \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e at the job level. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#jobsjob\_idconcurrency\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.concurrency\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis means that there can be at most one running and one pending job in a concurrency group at any time. When a concurrent job or workflow is queued, if another job or workflow using the same concurrency group in the repository is in progress, the queued job or workflow will be \u003ccode\u003epending\u003c/code\u003e. Any existing \u003ccode\u003epending\u003c/code\u003e job or workflow in the same concurrency group, if it exists, will be canceled and the new queued job or workflow will take its place.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo also cancel any currently running job or workflow in the same concurrency group, specify \u003ccode\u003ecancel-in-progress: true\u003c/code\u003e. To conditionally cancel currently running jobs or workflows in the same concurrency group, you can specify \u003ccode\u003ecancel-in-progress\u003c/code\u003e as an expression with any of the allowed expression contexts.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe concurrency group name is case insensitive. For example, \u003ccode\u003eprod\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eProd\u003c/code\u003e will be treated as the same concurrency group.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eOrdering is not guaranteed for jobs or workflow runs using concurrency groups. Jobs or workflow runs in the same concurrency group are handled in an arbitrary order.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-using-concurrency-and-the-default-behavior\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-using-concurrency-and-the-default-behavior\"\u003eExample: Using concurrency and the default behavior\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe default behavior of GitHub Actions is to allow multiple jobs or workflow runs to run concurrently. The \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e keyword allows you to control the concurrency of workflow runs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, you can use the \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e keyword immediately after where trigger conditions are defined to limit the concurrency of entire workflow runs for a specific branch:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.workflow\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}-${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can also limit the concurrency of jobs within a workflow by using the \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e keyword at the job level:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejob-1:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eruns-on:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eubuntu-latest\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eexample-group\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-concurrency-groups\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-concurrency-groups\"\u003eExample: Concurrency groups\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eConcurrency groups provide a way to manage and limit the execution of workflow runs or jobs that share the same concurrency key.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e key is used to group workflows or jobs together into a concurrency group. When you define a \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e key, GitHub Actions ensures that only one workflow or job with that key runs at any given time. If a new workflow run or job starts with the same \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e key, GitHub Actions will cancel any workflow or job already running with that key. The \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e key can be a hard-coded string, or it can be a dynamic expression that includes context variables.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIt is possible to define concurrency conditions in your workflow so that the workflow or job is part of a concurrency group.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis means that when a workflow run or job starts, GitHub will cancel any workflow runs or jobs that are already in progress in the same concurrency group. This is useful in scenarios where you want to prevent parallel runs for a certain set of a workflows or jobs, such as the ones used for deployments to a staging environment, in order to prevent actions that could cause conflicts or consume more resources than necessary.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn this example, \u003ccode\u003ejob-1\u003c/code\u003e is part of a concurrency group named \u003ccode\u003estaging\_environment\u003c/code\u003e. This means that if a new run of \u003ccode\u003ejob-1\u003c/code\u003e is triggered, any runs of the same job in the \u003ccode\u003estaging\_environment\u003c/code\u003e concurrency group that are already in progress will be cancelled.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejob-1:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eruns-on:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eubuntu-latest\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003estaging\_environment\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAlternatively, using a dynamic expression such as \u003ccode\u003econcurrency: ci-${{ github.ref }}\u003c/code\u003e in your workflow means that the workflow or job would be part of a concurrency group named \u003ccode\u003eci-\u003c/code\u003e followed by the reference of the branch or tag that triggered the workflow. In this example, if a new commit is pushed to the main branch while a previous run is still in progress, the previous run will be cancelled and the new one will start:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eci-${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-using-concurrency-to-cancel-any-in-progress-job-or-run\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-using-concurrency-to-cancel-any-in-progress-job-or-run\"\u003eExample: Using concurrency to cancel any in-progress job or run\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo use concurrency to cancel any in-progress job or run in GitHub Actions, you can use the \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e key with the \u003ccode\u003ecancel-in-progress\u003c/code\u003e option set to \u003ccode\u003etrue\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNote that in this example, without defining a particular concurrency group, GitHub Actions will cancel \u003cem\u003eany\u003c/em\u003e in-progress run of the job or workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-using-a-fallback-value\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-using-a-fallback-value\"\u003eExample: Using a fallback value\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you build the group name with a property that is only defined for specific events, you can use a fallback value. For example, \u003ccode\u003egithub.head\_ref\u003c/code\u003e is only defined on \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e events. If your workflow responds to other events in addition to \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e events, you will need to provide a fallback to avoid a syntax error. The following concurrency group cancels in-progress jobs or runs on \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e events only; if \u003ccode\u003egithub.head\_ref\u003c/code\u003e is undefined, the concurrency group will fallback to the run ID, which is guaranteed to be both unique and defined for the run.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.head\_ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e||\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.run\_id\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-only-cancel-in-progress-jobs-or-runs-for-the-current-workflow\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-only-cancel-in-progress-jobs-or-runs-for-the-current-workflow\"\u003eExample: Only cancel in-progress jobs or runs for the current workflow\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you have multiple workflows in the same repository, concurrency group names must be unique across workflows to avoid canceling in-progress jobs or runs from other workflows. Otherwise, any previously in-progress or pending job will be canceled, regardless of the workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo only cancel in-progress runs of the same workflow, you can use the \u003ccode\u003egithub.workflow\u003c/code\u003e property to build the concurrency group:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.workflow\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}-${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-only-cancel-in-progress-jobs-on-specific-branches\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-only-cancel-in-progress-jobs-on-specific-branches\"\u003eExample: Only cancel in-progress jobs on specific branches\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you would like to cancel in-progress jobs on certain branches but not on others, you can use conditional expressions with \u003ccode\u003ecancel-in-progress\u003c/code\u003e. For example, you can do this if you would like to cancel in-progress jobs on development branches but not on release branches.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo only cancel in-progress runs of the same workflow when not running on a release branch, you can set \u003ccode\u003ecancel-in-progress\u003c/code\u003e to an expression similar to the following:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.workflow\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}-${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-type\"\u003e!contains(github.ref,\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'release/'\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e)}}\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn this example, multiple pushes to a \u003ccode\u003erelease/1.2.3\u003c/code\u003e branch would not cancel in-progress runs. Pushes to another branch, such as \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e, would cancel in-progress runs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobs\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobs\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA workflow run is made up of one or more \u003ccode\u003ejobs\u003c/code\u003e, which run in parallel by default. To run jobs sequentially, you can define dependencies on other jobs using the \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.needs\u003c/code\u003e keyword.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEach job runs in a runner environment specified by \u003ccode\u003eruns-on\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can run an unlimited number of jobs as long as you are within the workflow usage limits. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/usage-limits-billing-and-administration\"\u003eBilling and usage\u003c/a\u003e for GitHub-hosted runners and \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/hosting-your-own-runners/managing-self-hosted-runners/usage-limits-for-self-hosted-runners\"\u003eActions limits\u003c/a\u003e for self-hosted runner usage limits.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you need to find the unique identifier of a job running in a workflow run, you can use the GitHub API. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/actions#workflow-jobs\"\u003eREST API endpoints for GitHub Actions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_id\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_id\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e\u003c/code\u003e to give your job a unique identifier. The key \u003ccode\u003ejob\_id\u003c/code\u003e is a string and its value is a map of the job's configuration data. You must replace \u003ccode\u003e\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e\u003c/code\u003e with a string that is unique to the \u003ccode\u003ejobs\u003c/code\u003e object. The \u003ccode\u003e\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e\u003c/code\u003e must start with a letter or \u003ccode\u003e\_\u003c/code\u003e and contain only alphanumeric characters, \u003ccode\u003e-\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003e\_\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-creating-jobs\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-creating-jobs\"\u003eExample: Creating jobs\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn this example, two jobs have been created, and their \u003ccode\u003ejob\_id\u003c/code\u003e values are \u003ccode\u003emy\_first\_job\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003emy\_second\_job\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ename:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eMy\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003esecond\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ejob\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idname\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.name\u003c/code\u003e to set a name for the job, which is href=\"#jobsjob\_idpermissions\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.permissions\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor a specific job, you can use \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.permissions\u003c/code\u003e to modify the default permissions granted to the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e, adding or removing access as required, so that you only allow the minimum required access. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/security-guides/automatic-token-authentication#modifying-the-permissions-for-the-github\_token\"\u003eUse GITHUB\_TOKEN for authentication in workflows\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBy specifying the permission within a job definition, you can configure a different set of permissions for the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e for each job, if required. Alternatively, you can specify the permissions for all jobs in the workflow. For information on defining permissions at the workflow level, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#permissions\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epermissions\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor each of the available permissions, shown in the table below, you can assign one of the access levels: \u003ccode\u003eread\u003c/code\u003e (if applicable), \u003ccode\u003ewrite\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003enone\u003c/code\u003e. \u003ccode\u003ewrite\u003c/code\u003e includes \u003ccode\u003eread\u003c/code\u003e. If you specify the access for any of these permissions, all of those that are not specified are set to \u003ccode\u003enone\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAvailable permissions and details of what each allows an action to do:\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\u003ctable aria-labelledby=\"jobsjob\_idpermissions\"\u003e\u003cthead\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003ePermission\u003c/th\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eAllows an action using \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e to\u003c/th\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003c/thead\u003e\u003ctbody\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003eactions\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eWork with GitHub Actions. For example, \u003ccode\u003estatuses:read\u003c/code\u003e permits an action to list the commit statuses for a given reference. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/overview/permissions-required-for-github-apps?apiVersion=2022-11-28#repository-permissions-for-commit-statuses\"\u003ePermissions required for GitHub Apps\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003c/tbody\u003e\u003c/table\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"defining-access-for-the-github\_token-scopes-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#defining-access-for-the-github\_token-scopes-1\"\u003eDefining access for the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e scopes\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can define the access that the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e will permit by specifying \u003ccode\u003eread\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003ewrite\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003enone\u003c/code\u003e as the value of the available permissions within the \u003ccode\u003epermissions\u003c/code\u003e key.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epermissions:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eactions:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eread|write|none\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eread|write|none\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003echecks:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eread|write|none\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econtents:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eread|write|none\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003edeployments:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eread|write|none\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ediscussions:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eread|write|none\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epackages:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eread|write|none\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epages:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eread|write|none\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epull-requests:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eread|write|none\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you specify the access for any of these permissions, all of those that are not specified are set to \u003ccode\u003enone\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use the following syntax to define one of \u003ccode\u003eread-all\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003ewrite-all\u003c/code\u003e access for all of the available permissions:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan permissions:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epermissions:\u003c/span\u003e {}\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"changing-the-permissions-in-a-forked-repository-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#changing-the-permissions-in-a-forked-repository-1\"\u003eChanging the permissions in a forked repository\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use the \u003ccode\u003epermissions\u003c/code\u003e key to add and remove read permissions for forked repositories, but typically you can't grant write access. The exception to this behavior is where an admin user has selected the \u003cstrong\u003eSend write tokens to workflows from pull requests\u003c/strong\u003e option in the GitHub Actions settings. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/repositories/managing-your-repositorys-settings-and-features/enabling-features-for-your-repository/managing-github-actions-settings-for-a-repository#enabling-workflows-for-private-repository-forks\"\u003eManaging GitHub Actions settings for a repository\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"example-setting-the-github\_token-permissions-for-one-job-in-a-workflow\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-setting-the-github\_token-permissions-for-one-job-in-a-workflow\"\u003eExample: Setting the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e permissions for one job in a workflow\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis example shows permissions being set for the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e that will only apply to the job named \u003ccode\u003estale\u003c/code\u003e. Write access is granted for the \u003ccode\u003eissues\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003epull-requests\u003c/code\u003e permissions. All other permissions will have no access.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003estale:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eruns-on:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eubuntu-latest\u003c/span\u003e\n\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epermissions:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eissues:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ewrite\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epull-requests:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ewrite\u003c/span\u003e\n\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003esteps:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003euses:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eactions/stale@v10\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idneeds\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idneeds\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.needs\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.needs\u003c/code\u003e to identify any jobs that must complete successfully before this job will run. It can be a string or array of strings. If a job fails or is skipped, all jobs that need it are skipped unless the jobs use a conditional expression that causes the job to continue. If a run contains a series of jobs that need each other, a failure or skip applies to all jobs in the dependency chain from the point of failure or skip onwards. If you would like a job to run even if a job it is dependent on did not succeed, use the \u003ccode\u003ealways()\u003c/code\u003e conditional expression in \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.if\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-requiring-successful-dependent-jobs\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-requiring-successful-dependent-jobs\"\u003eExample: Requiring successful dependent jobs\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejob1:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejob2:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eneeds:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ejob1\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejob3:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eneeds:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ejob1\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ejob2\u003c/span\u003e]\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn this example, \u003ccode\u003ejob1\u003c/code\u003e must complete successfully before \u003ccode\u003ejob2\u003c/code\u003e begins, and \u003ccode\u003ejob3\u003c/code\u003e waits for both \u003ccode\u003ejob1\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ejob2\u003c/code\u003e to complete.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe jobs in this example run sequentially:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejob1\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejob2\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejob3\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003ch3 successful dependent jobs\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ejob1\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ejob2\u003c/span\u003e]\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn this example, \u003ccode\u003ejob3\u003c/code\u003e uses the \u003ccode\u003ealways()\u003c/code\u003e conditional expression so that it always runs after \u003ccode\u003ejob1\u003c/code\u003e and For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/expressions#status-check-functions\"\u003eEvaluate expressions in workflows and actions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idif\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idif\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.if\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use the \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.if\u003c/code\u003e conditional to prevent a job from running unless a condition is met. However, this exception does not apply everywhere.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou must always use the \u003ccode\u003e${{ }}\u003c/code\u003e expression syntax or escape with \u003ccode\u003e''\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e\"\"\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003e()\u003c/code\u003e when the expression starts with \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e, since \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e is reserved notation in YAML format. href=\"#jobsjob\_idruns-on\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.runs-on\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.runs-on\u003c/code\u003e to define the type of machine to run the job on.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe destination machine can be either a \u003ca href=\"#choosing-github-hosted-runners\"\u003eGitHub-hosted runner\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"#choosing-runners-in-a-group\"\u003elarger runner\u003c/a\u003e, or a \u003ca href=\"#choosing-self-hosted-runners\"\u003eself-hosted runner\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can target runners based on the labels assigned to them, or their group membership, or a combination of these.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can provide \u003ccode\u003eruns-on\u003c/code\u003e as:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA single string\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA single variable containing a string\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAn array of strings, variables containing strings, or a combination of both\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eA \u003ccode\u003ekey: value\u003c/code\u003e pair using the \u003ccode\u003egroup\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003elabels\u003c/code\u003e keys\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you specify an array of strings or variables, your workflow will execute on any runner that matches all of the specified \u003ccode\u003eruns-on\u003c/code\u003e values. For example, here the job will only run on a self-hosted runner that has the labels \u003ccode\u003elinux\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003ex64\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003egpu\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eruns-on:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eself-hosted\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003elinux\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ex64\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egpu\u003c/span\u003e]\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor more information, see \u003ca href=\"#choosing-self-hosted-runners\"\u003eChoosing self-hosted runners\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can mix strings and variables in an array. For example:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eworkflow\_dispatch:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003einputs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003echosen-os:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003erequired:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003etype:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003echoice\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eoptions:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eUbuntu\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emacOS\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003etest:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eruns-on:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eself-hosted\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"$\u003cspan class=\"hljs-template-variable\"\u003e{{ inputs.chosen-os }}\u003c/span\u003e\"\u003c/span\u003e]\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003esteps:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003erun:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eecho\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eHello\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eworld!\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you would like to run your workflow on multiple machines, use \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#jobsjob\_idstrategy\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon around simple strings like \u003ccode\u003eself-hosted\u003c/code\u003e, but they are required for expressions like \u003ccode\u003e\"${{ inputs.chosen-os }}\"\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"choosing-github-hosted-runners\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#choosing-github-hosted-runners\"\u003eChoosing GitHub-hosted runners\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you use a GitHub-hosted runner, each job runs in a fresh instance of a runner image specified by \u003ccode\u003eruns-on\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe value for runs-on, when you are using a GitHub-hosted runner, is a runner label or the name of a runner group. The labels for the standard GitHub-hosted runners are shown in the following tables.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-github-hosted-runners/about-github-hosted-runners/about-github-hosted-runners\"\u003eGitHub-hosted runners\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"standard-github-hosted-runners-for-public-repositories\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#standard-github-hosted-runners-for-public-repositories\"\u003eStandard GitHub-hosted runners for public repositories\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor public repositories, jobs using the workflow labels shown in the table below will run with the associated specifications. With the exception of single-CPU runners, each GitHub-hosted runner is a new virtual machine (VM) hosted by GitHub. Single-CPU runners are hosted in a container on a shared VM—see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/reference/runners/github-hosted-runners#single-cpu-runners\"\u003eGitHub-hosted runners reference\u003c/a\u003e. Use of the standard GitHub-hosted runners is free and unlimited on public repositories.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\u003ctable style=\"width:100%\" Beta Images may not be covered by customer support.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"example-specifying-an-operating-system\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-specifying-an-operating-system\"\u003eExample: Specifying an operating system\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eruns-on:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eubuntu-latest\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-github-hosted-runners/about-github-hosted-runners\"\u003eGitHub-hosted runners\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"choosing-self-hosted-runners\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#choosing-self-hosted-runners\"\u003eChoosing self-hosted runners\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo specify a self-hosted runner for your job, configure \u003ccode\u003eruns-on\u003c/code\u003e in your workflow file with self-hosted runner labels.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSelf-hosted runners may have the \u003ccode\u003eself-hosted\u003c/code\u003e label. When setting up a self-hosted runner, by default we will include the label \u003ccode\u003eself-hosted\u003c/code\u003e. You may pass in the \u003ccode\u003e--no-default-labels\u003c/code\u003e flag to prevent the self-hosted label from being applied. Labels can be used to create targeting options for runners, such as operating system or architecture, we recommend providing an array of labels that begins with \u003ccode\u003eself-hosted\u003c/code\u003e (this must be listed first) and then includes additional labels as needed. When you specify an array of labels, jobs will be queued on runners that have all the labels that you specify.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eruns-on:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eself-hosted\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003elinux\u003c/span\u003e]\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/hosting-your-own-runners/managing-self-hosted-runners/about-self-hosted-runners\"\u003eSelf-hosted runners\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use \u003ccode\u003eruns-on\u003c/code\u003e to target runner groups, so that the job will execute on any runner that is a member of that group. For more granular control, you can also combine runner groups with labels.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eRunner groups can only have \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-github-hosted-runners/using-larger-runners/about-larger-runners\"\u003elarger runners\u003c/a\u003e or \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/how-tos/managing-self-hosted-runners\"\u003eself-hosted runners\u003c/a\u003e as members.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"example-using-groups-to-control-where-jobs-are-run\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-using-groups-to-control-where-jobs-are-run\"\u003eExample: Using groups to control where jobs are run\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn this example, Ubuntu runners have been added to a group called \u003ccode\u003eubuntu-runners\u003c/code\u003e. href=\"#example-combining-groups-and-labels\"\u003eExample: Combining groups and labels\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen you combine groups and labels, the runner must meet both requirements to be eligible to run the job.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn this example, a runner group called \u003ccode\u003eubuntu-runners\u003c/code\u003e is populated with Ubuntu runners, which have also been assigned the label \u003ccode\u003eubuntu-24.04-16core\u003c/code\u003e. The \u003ccode\u003eruns-on\u003c/code\u003e key combines \u003ccode\u003egroup\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003elabels\u003c/code\u003e so that the job is routed to any available runner within the group that also has a matching label:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ename:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan href=\"#jobsjob\_idsnapshot\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.snapshot\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.snapshot\u003c/code\u003e to generate a custom image.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAdd the snapshot keyword to the job, using either the string syntax or mapping syntax as shown in \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/how-tos/manage-runners/larger-runners/use-custom-images#generating-a-custom-image\"\u003eGenerating a custom image\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEach job that includes the snapshot keyword creates a separate image. To generate only one image or image version, include all workflow steps in a single job. Each successful run of a job that includes the snapshot keyword creates a new version of that image.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/how-tos/manage-runners/larger-runners/use-custom-images\"\u003eUsing custom images\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idenvironment\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idenvironment\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.environment\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.environment\u003c/code\u003e to define the environment that the job references.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can provide the environment as only the environment \u003ccode\u003ename\u003c/code\u003e, or as an environment object with the \u003ccode\u003ename\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eurl\u003c/code\u003e. The URL maps to \u003ccode\u003eenvironment\_url\u003c/code\u003e in the deployments API. For more information about the deployments API, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/repos#deployments\"\u003eREST API endpoints for repositories\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nAll deployment protection rules must pass before a job referencing the environment is sent to a runner. Allowed expression contexts: \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#github-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003egithub\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#inputs-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003einputs\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#vars-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003evars\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#needs-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eneeds\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#strategy-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003estrategy\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#matrix-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ematrix\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#job-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejob\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#runner-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003erunner\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#env-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eenv\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, and \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#steps-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003esteps\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e. Allowed expression contexts: \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#github-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003egithub\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#inputs-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003einputs\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#vars-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003evars\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#needs-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eneeds\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#strategy-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003estrategy\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, and \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#matrix-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ematrix\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e. as environment name\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-using-an-environment-without-creating-a-deployment\"\u003eExample: Using an environment without creating a deployment\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSet \u003ccode\u003edeployment\u003c/code\u003e to \u003ccode\u003efalse\u003c/code\u003e to use an environment's secrets and variables without creating a deployment object.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eenvironment:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ename:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003etesting\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003edeployment:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003efalse\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSetting \u003ccode\u003edeployment: false\u003c/code\u003e is not compatible with custom deployment protection rules.\nFor more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/how-tos/deploy/configure-and-manage-deployments/control-deployments#using-environments-without-deployments\"\u003eDeploying with GitHub Actions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idconcurrency\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idconcurrency\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.concurrency\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.concurrency\u003c/code\u003e to ensure that only a single job or workflow using the same concurrency group will run at a time. A concurrency group can be any string or expression. Allowed expression contexts: \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#github-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003egithub\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#inputs-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003einputs\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#vars-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003evars\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#needs-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eneeds\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#strategy-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003estrategy\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, and \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#matrix-context\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ematrix\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e. For more information about expressions, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/expressions\"\u003eEvaluate expressions in workflows and actions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can also specify \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e at the workflow level. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#concurrency\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis means that there can be at most one running and one pending job in a concurrency group at any time. When a concurrent job or workflow is queued, if another job or workflow using the same concurrency group in the repository is in progress, the queued job or workflow will be \u003ccode\u003epending\u003c/code\u003e. Any existing \u003ccode\u003epending\u003c/code\u003e job or workflow in the same concurrency group, if it exists, will be canceled and the new queued job or workflow will take its place.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo also cancel any currently running job or workflow in the same concurrency group, specify \u003ccode\u003ecancel-in-progress: true\u003c/code\u003e. To conditionally cancel currently running jobs or workflows in the same concurrency group, you can specify \u003ccode\u003ecancel-in-progress\u003c/code\u003e as an expression with any of the allowed expression contexts.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe concurrency group name is case insensitive. For example, \u003ccode\u003eprod\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eProd\u003c/code\u003e will be treated as the same concurrency group.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eOrdering is not guaranteed for jobs or workflow runs using concurrency groups. Jobs or workflow runs in the same concurrency group are handled in an arbitrary order.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-using-concurrency-and-the-default-behavior-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-using-concurrency-and-the-default-behavior-1\"\u003eExample: Using concurrency and the default behavior\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe default behavior of GitHub Actions is to allow multiple jobs or workflow runs to run concurrently. The \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e keyword allows you to control the concurrency of workflow runs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, you can use the \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e keyword immediately after where trigger conditions are defined to limit the concurrency of entire workflow runs for a specific branch:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.workflow\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}-${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can also limit the concurrency of jobs within a workflow by using the \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e keyword at the job level:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejob-1:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eruns-on:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eubuntu-latest\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eexample-group\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-concurrency-groups-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-concurrency-groups-1\"\u003eExample: Concurrency groups\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eConcurrency groups provide a way to manage and limit the execution of workflow runs or jobs that share the same concurrency key.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e key is used to group workflows or jobs together into a concurrency group. When you define a \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e key, GitHub Actions ensures that only one workflow or job with that key runs at any given time. If a new workflow run or job starts with the same \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e key, GitHub Actions will cancel any workflow or job already running with that key. The \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e key can be a hard-coded string, or it can be a dynamic expression that includes context variables.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIt is possible to define concurrency conditions in your workflow so that the workflow or job is part of a concurrency group.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis means that when a workflow run or job starts, GitHub will cancel any workflow runs or jobs that are already in progress in the same concurrency group. This is useful in scenarios where you want to prevent parallel runs for a certain set of a workflows or jobs, such as the ones used for deployments to a staging environment, in order to prevent actions that could cause conflicts or consume more resources than necessary.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn this example, \u003ccode\u003ejob-1\u003c/code\u003e is part of a concurrency group named \u003ccode\u003estaging\_environment\u003c/code\u003e. This means that if a new run of \u003ccode\u003ejob-1\u003c/code\u003e is triggered, any runs of the same job in the \u003ccode\u003estaging\_environment\u003c/code\u003e concurrency group that are already in progress will be cancelled.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejob-1:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eruns-on:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eubuntu-latest\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003estaging\_environment\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAlternatively, using a dynamic expression such as \u003ccode\u003econcurrency: ci-${{ github.ref }}\u003c/code\u003e in your workflow means that the workflow or job would be part of a concurrency group named \u003ccode\u003eci-\u003c/code\u003e followed by the reference of the branch or tag that triggered the workflow. In this example, if a new commit is pushed to the main branch while a previous run is still in progress, the previous run will be cancelled and the new one will start:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eon:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003epush:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ebranches:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emain\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eci-${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-using-concurrency-to-cancel-any-in-progress-job-or-run-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-using-concurrency-to-cancel-any-in-progress-job-or-run-1\"\u003eExample: Using concurrency to cancel any in-progress job or run\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo use concurrency to cancel any in-progress job or run in GitHub Actions, you can use the \u003ccode\u003econcurrency\u003c/code\u003e key with the \u003ccode\u003ecancel-in-progress\u003c/code\u003e option set to \u003ccode\u003etrue\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNote that in this example, without defining a particular concurrency group, GitHub Actions will cancel \u003cem\u003eany\u003c/em\u003e in-progress run of the job or workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-using-a-fallback-value-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-using-a-fallback-value-1\"\u003eExample: Using a fallback value\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you build the group name with a property that is only defined for specific events, you can use a fallback value. For example, \u003ccode\u003egithub.head\_ref\u003c/code\u003e is only defined on \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e events. If your workflow responds to other events in addition to \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e events, you will need to provide a fallback to avoid a syntax error. The following concurrency group cancels in-progress jobs or runs on \u003ccode\u003epull\_request\u003c/code\u003e events only; if \u003ccode\u003egithub.head\_ref\u003c/code\u003e is undefined, the concurrency group will fallback to the run ID, which is guaranteed to be both unique and defined for the run.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.head\_ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e||\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.run\_id\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-only-cancel-in-progress-jobs-or-runs-for-the-current-workflow-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-only-cancel-in-progress-jobs-or-runs-for-the-current-workflow-1\"\u003eExample: Only cancel in-progress jobs or runs for the current workflow\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you have multiple workflows in the same repository, concurrency group names must be unique across workflows to avoid canceling in-progress jobs or runs from other workflows. Otherwise, any previously in-progress or pending job will be canceled, regardless of the workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo only cancel in-progress runs of the same workflow, you can use the \u003ccode\u003egithub.workflow\u003c/code\u003e property to build the concurrency group:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.workflow\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}-${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-only-cancel-in-progress-jobs-on-specific-branches-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-only-cancel-in-progress-jobs-on-specific-branches-1\"\u003eExample: Only cancel in-progress jobs on specific branches\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you would like to cancel in-progress jobs on certain branches but not on others, you can use conditional expressions with \u003ccode\u003ecancel-in-progress\u003c/code\u003e. For example, you can do this if you would like to cancel in-progress jobs on development branches but not on release branches.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo only cancel in-progress runs of the same workflow when not running on a release branch, you can set \u003ccode\u003ecancel-in-progress\u003c/code\u003e to an expression similar to the following:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003econcurrency:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003egroup:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.workflow\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}-${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003egithub.ref\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecancel-in-progress:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-type\"\u003e!contains(github.ref,\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'release/'\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e)}}\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn this example, multiple pushes to a \u003ccode\u003erelease/1.2.3\u003c/code\u003e branch would not cancel in-progress runs. Pushes to another branch, such as \u003ccode\u003emain\u003c/code\u003e, would cancel in-progress runs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idoutputs\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idoutputs\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.outputs\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.outputs\u003c/code\u003e to create a \u003ccode\u003emap\u003c/code\u003e of outputs for a job. Job outputs are available to all downstream jobs that depend on this job. For more information on defining job dependencies, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#jobsjob\_idneeds\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.needs\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOutputs can be a maximum of 1 MB per job. The total of all outputs in a workflow run can be a maximum of 50 MB. Size is approximated based on UTF-16 encoding.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eJob outputs containing expressions are evaluated on the runner at the end of each job. Outputs containing secrets are redacted on the runner and not sent to GitHub Actions.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf an output is skipped because it may contain a secret, you will see the following warning message: \"Skip output \u003ccode\u003e{output.Key}\u003c/code\u003e since it may contain secret.\" For more information on how to handle secrets, please refer to the \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/writing-workflows/choosing-what-your-workflow-does/workflow-commands-for-github-actions#example-masking-and-passing-a-secret-between-jobs-or-workflows\"\u003eExample: Masking and passing a secret between jobs or workflows\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo use job outputs in a dependent job, you can use the \u003ccode\u003eneeds\u003c/code\u003e context. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#needs-context\"\u003eContexts reference\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003esteps.step2.outputs.test\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n When using a matrix, job outputs will be combined from all jobs inside the matrix.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M6.457 1.047c.659-1.234 2.427-1.234 3.086 0l6.082 11.378A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.082 15H1.918a1.75 1.75 0 0 1-1.543-2.575Zm1.763.707a.25.25 0 0 0-.44 0L1.698 13.132a.25.25 0 0 0 .22.368h12.164a.25.25 0 guarantee the order that matrix jobs will run in. Ensure that the output name is unique, otherwise the last matrix job that runs will override the output value.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idenv\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idenv\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.env\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA \u003ccode\u003emap\u003c/code\u003e of variables that are available to all steps in the job. You can set variables for the entire workflow or an individual step. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#env\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eenv\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#jobsjob\_idstepsenv\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.steps[\*].env\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen more than one environment variable is defined with the same name, GitHub uses the most specific variable. For example, an environment variable defined in a step will override job and workflow environment variables with the same name, while the step executes. An environment variable defined for a job will override a workflow variable with the same name, while the job executes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-of-jobsjob\_idenv\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-of-jobsjob\_idenv\"\u003eExample of \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.env\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejob1:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eenv:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eFIRST\_NAME:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eMona\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_iddefaults\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_iddefaults\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.defaults\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.defaults\u003c/code\u003e to create a \u003ccode\u003emap\u003c/code\u003e of default settings that will apply to all steps in the job. You can also set default settings for the entire workflow. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-workflows/workflow-syntax-for-github-actions#defaults\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003edefaults\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen more than one default setting is defined with the same name, GitHub uses the most specific default setting. Steps can run commands, run setup tasks, or run an action in your repository, a public repository, or an action published in a Docker registry. Not all steps run actions, but all actions run as a step. Each step runs in its own process in the runner environment and has access to the workspace and filesystem. Because steps run in their own process, changes to environment variables are not preserved between steps. GitHub provides built-in steps to set up and complete a job.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eGitHub only displays the first 1,000 checks, however, you can run an unlimited number of steps as long as you are within the workflow usage limits. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/usage-limits-billing-and-administration\"\u003eBilling and usage\u003c/a\u003e for GitHub-hosted runners and \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/hosting-your-own-runners/managing-self-hosted-runners/usage-limits-for-self-hosted-runners\"\u003eActions limits\u003c/a\u003e for self-hosted runner usage limits.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-of-jobsjob\_idsteps\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-of-jobsjob\_idsteps\"\u003eExample of You can use any supported context and expression to create a conditional. For more information on which contexts are supported in this key, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts#context-availability\"\u003eContexts reference\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen you use expressions in an \u003ccode\u003eif\u003c/code\u003e conditional, you can, optionally, omit the \u003ccode\u003e${{ }}\u003c/code\u003e expression syntax because GitHub Actions automatically evaluates the \u003ccode\u003eif\u003c/code\u003e conditional as an expression. However, this exception does not apply everywhere.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou must always use the \u003ccode\u003e${{ }}\u003c/code\u003e expression syntax or escape with \u003ccode\u003e''\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e\"\"\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003e()\u003c/code\u003e when the expression starts with \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e, since \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e is reserved notation in YAML format. For example:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eif:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan
