class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA name for your step to display on GitHub.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idstepsuses\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstepsuses\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.steps[\*].uses\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSelects an action to run as part of a step in your job. An action is a reusable unit of code. You can use an action defined in the same repository as the workflow, a public repository, or in a \u003ca href=\"https://hub.docker.com/\"\u003epublished Docker container image\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWe strongly recommend that you include the version of the action you are using by specifying a Git ref, SHA, or Docker tag. If you don't specify a version, it could break your workflows or cause unexpected behavior when the action owner publishes an update.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eUsing the commit SHA of a released action version is the safest for stability and security.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf the action publishes major version tags, you should expect to receive critical fixes and security patches while still retaining compatibility. Note that this behavior is at the discretion of the action's author.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eUsing the default branch of an action may be convenient, but if someone releases a new major version with a breaking change, your workflow could break.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSome actions require inputs that you must set using the \u003ca href=\"#jobsjob\_idstepswith\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ewith\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e keyword. Review the action's README file to determine the inputs required.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eActions are either JavaScript files or Docker containers. If the action you're using is a Docker container you must run the job in a Linux environment. For more details, see \u003ca href=\"#jobsjob\_idruns-on\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eruns-on\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-using-versioned-actions\" class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor built-in shell keywords, we provide the following defaults that are executed by GitHub-hosted runners. You should use these guidelines when running shell scripts.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ccode\u003ebash\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003esh\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eBy default, fail-fast behavior is enforced using \u003ccode\u003eset -e\u003c/code\u003e for both \u003ccode\u003esh\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ebash\u003c/code\u003e. When \u003ccode\u003eshell: bash\u003c/code\u003e is specified, \u003ccode\u003e-o pipefail\u003c/code\u003e is also applied to enforce early exit from pipelines that generate a non-zero exit status.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eYou can take full control over shell parameters by providing a template string to the shell options. For example, \u003ccode\u003ebash {0}\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003esh\u003c/code\u003e-like shells exit with the exit code of the last command executed in a script, which is also the default behavior for actions. The runner will report the status of the step as fail/succeed based on this exit code.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ccode\u003epowershell\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003epwsh\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eFail-fast behavior when possible. For \u003ccode\u003epwsh\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003epowershell\u003c/code\u003e built-in shell, we will prepend \u003ccode\u003e$ErrorActionPreference = 'stop'\u003c/code\u003e to script contents.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWe append \u003ccode\u003eif ((Test-Path -LiteralPath variable:\\LASTEXITCODE)) { exit $LASTEXITCODE }\u003c/code\u003e to powershell scripts so action statuses reflect the script's last exit code.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eUsers can always opt out by not using the built-in shell, and providing a custom shell option like: \u003ccode\u003epwsh -File {0}\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003epowershell -Command \"\u0026#x26; '{0}'\"\u003c/code\u003e, depending on need.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ccode\u003ecmd\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThere doesn't seem to be a way to fully opt into fail-fast behavior other than writing your script to check each error code and respond accordingly. Because we can't actually provide that behavior by default, you need to write this behavior into your script.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ecmd.exe\u003c/code\u003e will exit with the error level of the last program it executed, and it will return the error code to the runner. This behavior is internally consistent with the previous \u003ccode\u003esh\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003epwsh\u003c/code\u003e default behavior and is the \u003ccode\u003ecmd.exe\u003c/code\u003e default, so this behavior remains intact.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idstepswith\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstepswith\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.steps[\*].with\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA \u003ccode\u003emap\u003c/code\u003e of the input parameters defined by the action. If you use \u003ccode\u003eCMD\u003c/code\u003e in your \u003ccode\u003eDockerfile\u003c/code\u003e, use the guidelines ordered by preference:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eDocument required arguments in the action's README and omit them from the \u003ccode\u003eCMD\u003c/code\u003e instruction.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eUse defaults that allow using the action without specifying any \u003ccode\u003eargs\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf the action exposes a \u003ccode\u003e--help\u003c/code\u003e flag, or something similar, use that as the default to make your action self-documenting.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idstepswithentrypoint\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstepswithentrypoint\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.steps[\*].with.entrypoint\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOverrides the Docker \u003ccode\u003eENTRYPOINT\u003c/code\u003e in the \u003ccode\u003eDockerfile\u003c/code\u003e, or sets it if one wasn't already specified. \u003ccode\u003eentrypoint\u003c/code\u003e keyword is meant to be used with Docker container actions, but you can also use it with JavaScript actions that don't define any inputs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idstepsenv\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstepsenv\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.steps[\*].env\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSets variables for steps to use in the runner environment. You can also set variables for the entire workflow or a job. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#env\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eenv\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#jobsjob\_idenv\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.env\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen more than one environment variable is defined with the same name, GitHub uses the most specific variable. For example, an environment variable defined in a step will override job and workflow environment variables with the same name, while the step executes. An environment variable defined for a job will override a workflow variable with the same name, while the job executes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003ePublic actions may specify expected variables in the README file. If you are setting a secret or sensitive value, such as a password or token, you must set secrets using the \u003ccode\u003esecrets\u003c/code\u003e context. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts\"\u003eContexts reference\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-of-jobsjob\_idstepsenv\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-of-jobsjob\_idstepsenv\"\u003eExample of \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.steps[\*].env\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003esteps:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ename:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eMy\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003efirst\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eaction\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eenv:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003esecrets.GITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eFIRST\_NAME:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eMona\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eLAST\_NAME:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eOctocat\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idstepscontinue-on-error\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstepscontinue-on-error\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.steps[\*].continue-on-error\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003ePrevents a job from failing when a step fails. Set to \u003ccode\u003etrue\u003c/code\u003e to allow a job to pass when this step fails.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idstepstimeout-minutes\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstepstimeout-minutes\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.steps[\*].timeout-minutes\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe maximum number of minutes to run the step before killing the process. Maximum: 360 for both GitHub-hosted and self-hosted runners.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFractional values are not supported. \u003ccode\u003etimeout-minutes\u003c/code\u003e must be a positive integer.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idtimeout-minutes\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idtimeout-minutes\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.timeout-minutes\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe maximum number of minutes to let a job run before GitHub automatically cancels it. Default: 360\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf the timeout exceeds the job execution time limit for the runner, the job will be canceled when the execution time limit is met instead. For more information about job execution time limits, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/usage-limits-billing-and-administration#usage-limits\"\u003eBilling and usage\u003c/a\u003e for GitHub-hosted runners and \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/hosting-your-own-runners/managing-self-hosted-runners/usage-limits-for-self-hosted-runners\"\u003eActions limits\u003c/a\u003e for self-hosted runner usage limits.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nThe \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e expires when a job finishes or after a maximum of 24 hours. For self-hosted runners, the token may be the limiting factor if the job timeout is greater than 24 hours. For more information on the \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB\_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/security-guides/automatic-token-authentication#about-the-github\_token-secret\"\u003eUse GITHUB\_TOKEN for authentication in workflows\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idstrategy\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstrategy\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy\u003c/code\u003e to use a matrix strategy for your jobs. A matrix strategy lets you use variables in a single job definition to automatically create multiple job runs that are based on the combinations of the variables. For example, you can use a matrix strategy to test your code in multiple versions of a language or on multiple operating systems. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-jobs/using-a-matrix-for-your-jobs\"\u003eRunning variations of jobs in a workflow\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idstrategymatrix\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstrategymatrix\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy.matrix\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy.matrix\u003c/code\u003e to define a matrix of different job configurations. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/how-tos/writing-workflows/choosing-what-your-workflow-does/running-variations-of-jobs-in-a-workflow\"\u003eRunning variations of jobs in a workflow\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA matrix will generate a maximum of 256 jobs per workflow run. This limit applies to both GitHub-hosted and self-hosted runners.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe variables that you define become properties in the \u003ccode\u003ematrix\u003c/code\u003e context, and you can reference the property in other areas of your workflow file. In this example, you can use \u003ccode\u003ematrix.version\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ematrix.os\u003c/code\u003e to access the current value of \u003ccode\u003eversion\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eos\u003c/code\u003e that the job is using. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/learn-github-actions/contexts\"\u003eContexts reference\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBy default, GitHub will maximize the number of jobs run in parallel depending on runner availability. The order of the variables in the matrix determines the order in which the jobs are created. The first variable you define will be the first job that is created in your workflow run.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"using-a-single-dimension-matrix\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#using-a-single-dimension-matrix\"\u003eUsing a single-dimension matrix\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe following workflow defines the variable \u003ccode\u003eversion\u003c/code\u003e with the values \u003ccode\u003e[10, 12, 14]\u003c/code\u003e. The workflow will run three jobs, one for each value in the variable. Each job will access the \u003ccode\u003eversion\u003c/code\u003e value through the \u003ccode\u003ematrix.version\u003c/code\u003e context and pass the value as \u003ccode\u003enode-version\u003c/code\u003e to the \u003ccode\u003eactions/setup-node\u003c/code\u003e action.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eexample\_matrix:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003estrategy:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ematrix:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eversion:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e10\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e12\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e14\u003c/span\u003e]\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003esteps:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003euses:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eactions/setup-node@v4\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ewith:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003enode-version:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ematrix.version\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"using-a-multi-dimensional-matrix\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#using-a-multi-dimensional-matrix\"\u003eUsing a multi-dimensional matrix\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSpecify multiple variables to create a multi-dimensional matrix. A job will run for each possible combination of the variables.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the following workflow specifies two variables:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eTwo operating systems specified in the \u003ccode\u003eos\u003c/code\u003e variable\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThree Node.js versions specified in the \u003ccode\u003eversion\u003c/code\u003e variable\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe workflow will run six jobs, one for each combination of the \u003ccode\u003eos\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eversion\u003c/code\u003e variables. to the \u003ccode\u003eactions/setup-node\u003c/code\u003e action.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstrategymatrixinclude\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy.matrix.include\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor each object in the \u003ccode\u003einclude\u003c/code\u003e list, the key:value pairs in the object will be added to each of the matrix combinations if none of the key:value pairs overwrite any of the original matrix values. If the object cannot be added to any of the matrix combinations, a new matrix combination will be created instead. Note that the original matrix values will not be overwritten, but added matrix values can be overwritten.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-expanding-configurations\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-expanding-configurations\"\u003eExample: Expanding configurations\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the following workflow will run four jobs, one for each combination of \u003ccode\u003eos\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003enode\u003c/code\u003e. When the job for the \u003ccode\u003eos\u003c/code\u003e value of \u003ccode\u003ewindows-latest\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003enode\u003c/code\u003e value of \u003ccode\u003e16\u003c/code\u003e runs, an additional variable called \u003ccode\u003enpm\u003c/code\u003e with the value of \u003ccode\u003e6\u003c/code\u003e will be included in the job.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode href=\"#example-adding-configurations\"\u003eExample: Adding configurations\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, this matrix will run 10 jobs, one for each combination of \u003ccode\u003eos\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eversion\u003c/code\u003e in the matrix, plus a job for the \u003ccode\u003eos\u003c/code\u003e value of \u003ccode\u003ewindows-latest\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eversion\u003c/code\u003e value of \u003ccode\u003e17\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eexample\_matrix:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003estrategy:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ematrix:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eos:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003emacos-latest\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ewindows-latest\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eubuntu-latest\u003c/span\u003e]\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eversion:\u003c/span\u003e [\u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e12\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e14\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e16\u003c/span\u003e]\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003einclude:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eos:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ewindows-latest\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eversion:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e17\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you don't specify any matrix variables, all configurations under \u003ccode\u003einclude\u003c/code\u003e will run. For example, the following workflow would run two jobs, one for each \u003ccode\u003einclude\u003c/code\u003e entry. This lets you take advantage of the matrix strategy without having a fully populated matrix.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eincludes\_only:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eruns-on:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eubuntu-latest\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003estrategy:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ematrix:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003einclude:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003esite:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"production\"\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003edatacenter:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"site-a\"\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-bullet\"\u003e-\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003esite:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"staging\"\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003edatacenter:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"site-b\"\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idstrategymatrixexclude\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstrategymatrixexclude\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy.matrix.exclude\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAn excluded configuration only has to be a partial match for it to be excluded.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAll \u003ccode\u003einclude\u003c/code\u003e combinations are processed after \u003ccode\u003eexclude\u003c/code\u003e. This allows you to use \u003ccode\u003einclude\u003c/code\u003e to add back combinations that were previously excluded.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idstrategyfail-fast\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#jobsjob\_idstrategyfail-fast\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy.fail-fast\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can control how job failures are handled with \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy.fail-fast\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.continue-on-error\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy.fail-fast\u003c/code\u003e applies to the entire matrix. If \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy.fail-fast\u003c/code\u003e is set to \u003ccode\u003etrue\u003c/code\u003e or its expression evaluates to \u003ccode\u003etrue\u003c/code\u003e, GitHub will cancel all in-progress and queued jobs in the matrix if any job in the matrix fails. This property defaults to \u003ccode\u003etrue\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.continue-on-error\u003c/code\u003e applies to a single job. If \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.continue-on-error\u003c/code\u003e is \u003ccode\u003etrue\u003c/code\u003e, other jobs in the matrix will continue running even if the job with \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.continue-on-error: true\u003c/code\u003e fails.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.strategy.fail-fast\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.continue-on-error\u003c/code\u003e together. For example, the following workflow will start four jobs. For each job, \u003ccode\u003econtinue-on-error\u003c/code\u003e is determined by the value of \u003ccode\u003ematrix.experimental\u003c/code\u003e. If any of the jobs with \u003ccode\u003econtinue-on-error: false\u003c/code\u003e fail, all jobs that are in progress or queued will be cancelled. If the job with \u003ccode\u003econtinue-on-error: true\u003c/code\u003e fails, the other jobs will not be affected.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e${{\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003ematrix.experimental\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e}}\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003estrategy:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003efail-fast:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-literal\"\u003etrue\u003c/span\u003e\n 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nIf your workflows use Docker container actions, job containers, or service containers, then you must use a Linux runner:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf you are using GitHub-hosted runners, you must use an Ubuntu runner.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf you are using self-hosted runners, you must use a Linux machine as your runner and Docker must be installed.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUsed to host service containers for a job in a workflow. Service containers are useful for creating databases or cache services like Redis. The runner automatically creates a Docker network and manages the life cycle of the service containers.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you configure your job to run in a container, or your step uses container actions, you don't need to map ports to access the service or action. Docker automatically exposes all ports between containers on the same Docker user-defined bridge network. You can directly reference the service container by its hostname. The hostname is automatically mapped to the label name you configure for the service in the workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you configure the job to run directly on the runner machine and your step doesn't use a container action, you must map any required Docker service container ports to the Docker host (the runner machine). You can access the service container using localhost and the mapped port.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor more information about the differences between networking service containers, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/using-containerized-services/about-service-containers\"\u003eCommunicating with Docker service containers\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-using-localhost\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-using-localhost\"\u003eExample: Using localhost\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis example creates two services: nginx and redis. When you specify the container port but not the host port, the container port is randomly assigned to a free port on the host. GitHub sets the assigned host port in the \u003ccode\u003e${{job.services.\u0026#x3C;service\_name\u003e.ports}}\u003c/code\u003e context. In this example, you can access the service host ports using the \u003ccode\u003e${{ job.services.nginx.ports['80'] }}\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e${{ job.services.redis.ports['6379'] }}\u003c/code\u003e contexts.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eservices:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003e# Map port 8080 on the Docker host to port 80 on the nginx container\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eports:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eredis:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003eimage:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003eredis\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e|\n echo \"Redis available on 127.0.0.1:${{ job.services.redis.ports['6379'] }}\"\n echo \"Nginx available on 127.0.0.1:${{ job.services.nginx.ports['80'] }}\"\n\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"jobsjob\_idservicesservice\_idimage\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Docker image to use as the service container to run the action. The value can be the Docker Hub image name or a registry name.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.services.\u0026#x3C;service\_id\u003e.image\u003c/code\u003e is assigned an empty string, the service will not start. Use one of the following syntaxes:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e{owner}/{repo}/.github/workflows/{filename}@{ref}\u003c/code\u003e for reusable workflows in public and private repositories.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e./.github/workflows/{filename}\u003c/code\u003e for reusable workflows in the same repository.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn the first option, \u003ccode\u003e{ref}\u003c/code\u003e can be a SHA, a release tag, or a branch name. If a release tag and a branch have the same name, the release tag takes precedence over the branch name. Using the commit SHA is the safest option for stability and security. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/actions/security-guides/security-hardening-for-github-actions#reusing-third-party-workflows\"\u003eSecure use reference\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you use the second syntax option (without \u003ccode\u003e{owner}/{repo}\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e@{ref}\u003c/code\u003e) the called workflow is from the same commit as the caller workflow. Ref prefixes such as \u003ccode\u003erefs/heads\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003erefs/tags\u003c/code\u003e are not allowed. You cannot use contexts or expressions in this keyword.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"example-of-jobsjob\_iduses\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-of-jobsjob\_iduses\"\u003eExample of \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.uses\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ejobs:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003ecall-workflow-1-in-local-repo:\u003c/span\u003e\n \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003euses:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen a job is used to call a reusable workflow, you can use \u003ccode\u003ewith\u003c/code\u003e to provide a map of inputs that are passed to the called workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAny inputs that you pass must match the input specifications defined in the called workflow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUnlike \u003ca href=\"#jobsjob\_idstepswith\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.steps[\*].with\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e, the inputs you pass with \u003ccode\u003ejobs.\u0026#x3C;job\_id\u003e.with\u003c/code\u003e are not available as environment variables in the called workflow. aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA pair consisting of a string identifier for the secret and the value of the secret. For example, \u003ccode\u003eOcto\*\u003c/code\u003e matches \u003ccode\u003eOctocat\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e\*\*\u003c/code\u003e: Matches zero or more of any character.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e?\u003c/code\u003e: Matches zero or one of the preceding character.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e+\u003c/code\u003e: Matches one or more of the preceding character.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e[]\u003c/code\u003e Matches one alphanumeric character listed in the brackets or included in ranges. Ranges can only include \u003ccode\u003ea-z\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eA-Z\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003e0-9\u003c/code\u003e. For example, the range\u003ccode\u003e[0-9a-z]\u003c/code\u003e matches any digit or lowercase letter. For example, \u003ccode\u003e[CB]at\u003c/code\u003e matches \u003ccode\u003eCat\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003eBat\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e[1-2]00\u003c/code\u003e matches \u003ccode\u003e100\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e200\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e: At the start of a pattern makes it negate previous positive patterns. It has no special meaning if not the first character.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe characters \u003ccode\u003e\*\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e[\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e are special characters in YAML. If you start a pattern with \u003ccode\u003e\*\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e[\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e, you must enclose the pattern in quotes. Also, if you use a \u003ca href=\"https://yaml.org/spec/1.2.2/#flow-sequences\"\u003eflow sequence\u003c/a\u003e with a pattern containing \u003ccode\u003e[\u003c/code\u003e and/or \u003ccode\u003e]\u003c/code\u003e, the pattern must be enclosed in quotes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-yaml\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003e# id=\"patterns-to-match-file-paths\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#patterns-to-match-file-paths\"\u003ePatterns to match file paths\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003ePath patterns must match the whole path, and start from the repository's root.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\u003ctable aria-labelledby=\"patterns-to-match-file-paths\"\u003e\u003cthead\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003ePattern\u003c/th\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eDescription of matches\u003c/th\u003e\u003cth scope=\"col\"\u003eExample matches\u003c/th\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003c/thead\u003e\u003ctbody\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003e\*\u003c/code\u003e wildcard matches any character, but does not match slash (\u003ccode\u003e/\u003c/code\u003e). The \u003ccode\u003e\*\u003c/code\u003e character is a special character in YAML. When you start a pattern with \u003ccode\u003e\*\u003c/code\u003e, you must use quotes.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003eREADME.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003eserver.rb\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*.jsx?'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003e?\u003c/code\u003e character matches zero or one of the preceding character.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003epage.js\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003epage.jsx\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*\*'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003e\*\*\u003c/code\u003e wildcard matches any character including slash (\u003ccode\u003e/\u003c/code\u003e). This is the default behavior when you don't use a \u003ccode\u003epath\u003c/code\u003e filter.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003eall/the/files.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*.js'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003e\*\u003c/code\u003e wildcard matches any character, but does not match slash (\u003ccode\u003e/\u003c/code\u003e). Matches all \u003ccode\u003e.js\u003c/code\u003e files at the root of the repository.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003eapp.js\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003eindex.js\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*\*.js'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eMatches all \u003ccode\u003e.js\u003c/code\u003e files in the repository.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003eindex.js\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejs/index.js\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003esrc/js/app.js\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/\*\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eAll files within the root of the \u003ccode\u003edocs\u003c/code\u003e directory only, at the root of the repository.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/README.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/file.txt\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/\*\*\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eAny files in the \u003ccode\u003edocs\u003c/code\u003e directory and its subdirectories at the root of the repository.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/README.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/mona/octocat.txt\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/\*\*/\*.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eA file with a \u003ccode\u003e.md\u003c/code\u003e suffix anywhere in the \u003ccode\u003edocs\u003c/code\u003e directory.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/README.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/mona/hello-world.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/a/markdown/file.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*\*/docs/\*\*'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eAny files in a \u003ccode\u003edocs\u003c/code\u003e directory anywhere in the repository.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/hello.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003edir/docs/my-file.txt\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003espace/docs/plan/space.doc\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*\*/README.md'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eA README.md file anywhere in the repository.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003eREADME.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003ejs/README.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*\*/\*src/\*\*'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eAny file in a folder with a \u003ccode\u003esrc\u003c/code\u003e suffix anywhere in the repository.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003ea/src/app.js\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003emy-src/code/js/app.js\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*\*/\*-post.md'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eA file with the suffix \u003ccode\u003e-post.md\u003c/code\u003e anywhere in the repository.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003emy-post.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003epath/their-post.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*\*/migrate-\*.sql'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eA file with the prefix \u003ccode\u003emigrate-\u003c/code\u003e and suffix \u003ccode\u003e.sql\u003c/code\u003e anywhere in the repository.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003emigrate-10909.sql\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003edb/migrate-v1.0.sql\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003edb/sept/migrate-v1.sql\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*.md'\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'!README.md'\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003eUsing an exclamation mark (\u003ccode\u003e!\u003c/code\u003e) in front of a pattern negates it. When a file matches a pattern and also matches a negative pattern defined later in the file, the file will not be included.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003ehello.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cem\u003eDoes not match\u003c/em\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003eREADME.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003edocs/hello.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003ctr\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'\*.md'\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003e'!README.md'\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003eREADME\*\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003ePatterns are checked sequentially. A pattern that negates a previous pattern will re-include file paths.\u003c/td\u003e\u003ctd\u003e\u003ccode\u003ehello.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003eREADME.md\u003c/code\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ccode\u003eREADME.doc\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/td\u003e\u003c/tr\u003e\u003c/tbody\u003e\u003c/table\u003e","miniTocItems":[{"contents":{"href":"#about-yaml-syntax-for-workflows","title":"About
